=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Camel up. Or, as I like to call it, the middle eastern OTB, is a surprisingly good play. I wanted to dismiss this game when I heard it beat Splendor for the spiel. At the time I remember thinking, "I need to at least try it to see why a racing game would beat splendor". So yeah, Splendor. Anyways, what I found out was that Camel Up is a fantastic game that has nothing to do with racing. I mean, there is a race going on and the camel meeples do race around the board but the game is actually a betting game. You spend the entire game making short term "leg" bets, long term race outcome bets, manipulating the track to alter the outcome of a particular leg, and eventually making a pyramid poop out a die to share information that will make the next players choices slightly more informed. Don't let the race cover or the apparent camel on camel porn dissuade you from trying this out because it is fast, fun, and scales very nicely up to 8 players. Splendor? Who cares about Splendor? I need to place a bet on Mossy humps to go all the way! Yip yip!

RATING: 8
I heard of Camel Up for the first time directly when it was nominated for the Spiel des Jahres. So I was really curious, because nobody was talking about this game at the time! I looked it up and what I saw was a weird chaotic game... that seemed completely impossible to control and I really couldn't understand the choice of the committee. So I just stopped caring about it, even when it won the prize. Many months later it casually happened that I had the opportunity to play it. Now I understand why the committee made that choice and I've to say, that they absolutely made the right call!

It's true that the game is light and chaotic, but the SdJ is a family oriented prize and this game is just perfect for that crowd! Camel Up shouldn't be approached as a game in which you have to build strategies, count your moves or your chances. It's about pushing your luck, making crazy bets and having some silly fun with a bunch of people... and the game works great for all of that. The components are really cool too and especially the pyramid, which may look weird but it definitively makes the game unique and more fun.

Overall a silly game with a silly theme, that just works and does exactly what it should do. It delivers laughter, excitement, a great social experience and it works really well with families and casual players.  I've never seen a group cheering, shouting and laughing playing Splendor... but I've seen that happening when they were playing Camel Up. That is the seal of the better family game, no matter how much better Splendor is selling. Don't skip this one just due to its randomness, because I liked a lot more than I thought I would have.

RATING: 6
Das Spiel ist ein eher chaotisches Kamelrennen. Zu planen gibt es wenig bis gar nichts. Konkreten Einfluss auf den Rennverlauf hat man kaum. Der Schwerpunkt liegt darin abzuschätzen, wie die jeweilige Etappe und das gesamte Rennen wohl ausgehen könnten. Dabei führen sowohl der Würfelmechanismus als solcher als auch der Zugmechanismus dazu, dass eine einigermaßen verlässliche Voraussage nur in seltenen Spielsituationen möglich ist. Durchaus nett, wenn es gespielt wird als schnelle, lustige Zockerei. Grübeln ist da sinnlos, tötet nur den Spielspaß. Merkwürdig, dass zweimal hintereinander Zockerspiele Spiel des Jahres geworden sind, wobei "Spiel des Jahres" aktuell per definitionem ein Familienspiel mit einfachem Einstieg, leicht verständlichen Regeln und geringem Schwierigkeitsgrad ist. Das war nicht immer so, sonst hätten Spiele wie Catan und El Grande vor rund 20 Jahren nicht Spiel des Jahres werden können; heutzutage könnten solche Spiele bestenfalls noch Kennerspiel des Jahres werden oder fielen komplett aus der Wertung für diese Preise raus; solchen Spielen könnte allenfalls noch der Deutsche Spielepreis winken, wenn sie denn dafür bekannt genug sind.

RATING: 4
Look, I'm not some joyless bean-counting efficiency gamer.  I can enjoy a thirty minute romp that is high on the luck scale.  While I am assuredly not the target market for Camel Up, I might have had fun.  It does have the neat mechanism of camels hitching a ride on other camels to raise it above straightforward roll and move.  It does have the gimmick of the pyramid dice shaker. Yet it fell very flat with me.  I think that's because, rather than letting me relax and enjoy some dumb fun, it invites me to think like a gamer, assessing options for my turn and calculating odds...before it kicks me in the nuts with pure blind luck. 

Production quality is very good; the pyramid seems durable and the camels are chunky and stack well.  The artwork made little impression, either positive or negative.

RATING: 6

The trick is to determine when to bet on certain colors winning legs of the race, and ultimately, winning the entire race.  I find this game to be clever, but not particularly compelling or fun beyond learning how to react to dice rolls.  Curiously, I feel I should like this game more than I do.  Perhaps on future plays, it will improve.

I don't want to overstate the decisions and/or understate the influence of the randomness. But for something so simple, quick, and accessible to different player counts... it's a game I'll keep in my collection for some time.

RATING: 6.5
A family targeted racing and betting game. Five camels race on a circular track, and players place bets on the winner of each leg, and overall winner and loser.

The game is very light, and I see it can hardly work with strategic players (the first turns of each leg there is little information available, so the best move is draw a die from the pyramid, but after 2-3 dice have been drawn, the next one will give away too much, so everyone tries to avoid drawing…), but with the casual/family gamers is a sure hit, and after playing it more than 10 times in a week during a holiday with casual gamers, I admit it deserved the Spiel des Jahres!

I gave away my copy as a gift after that holiday, and now I will probably get another...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
It's easy to see why this game scooped the Spiel des Jahres - the whole family was instantly hooked.

You play a member of Egyptian high society betting on a camel race.  Each turn you can do one of four things - move a camel, bet on a camel to win a leg (a leg is a segment of the race completed when all 5 camels have moved), place your oasis/mirage tile to boost/reduce the movement of any camel that lands on it or bet on the eventual winner or last place finisher in the race. 

Camels are moved using a cardboard pyramid which contains the 5 coloured dice (one for each camel). You give it shake, turn it upside down and then push a little cardboard door open to release a die onto the board.

The winner is the person with the most money at the end of race.  Money is awarded at the end of each leg, and once one of the camels has crossed the finish line.

The fun is that the race is so unpredictable. That's because any camel that lands on the same space as another camel hops on top of it and moves with it when it moves. So a camel can be well behind the leader, get a couple of piggybacks and move into contention. We've had more than a couple of 5 camels stacks, and one instance of a camel I'd bet on to to finish last coming first.

Each turn you have interesting decisions.  If you use your action to move a camel, you'll have more of an idea who'll win the leg but your opponents will be able to bet on the leg winner before you have a chance (only 3 people can bet on a single camel to win a leg). If you bet early in the leg, before most of the camels have moved, the rewards are potentially greater but you've got less chance of picking the leg winner.

It strikes a great balance between luck and strategy, which makes the game a great good leveller between kids and their smart arse parents.

My only complaint would be the dice pyramid. Its a great little device, and the kids love it, but I broke my first rubber band in game 2. I have 2 spares (well, 1 now) but the rate of attrition doesn't bode well.

For the kids, it would also be great to have names and profiles for the 'betters' - and perhaps unique abilities - it just adds another dimension to the game.

On the flipside, the components are very high quality and the game is very well priced.

All in all a great game for a family or a group of friends. You'll find yourself wanting to play again as soon as you've finished.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Camel Up is a combined race and betting game.  I love the way you almost play a game of chicken with everyone else, hoping they will be the one to roll the dice so that you can be the one to make the more accurate bets.  The way the camels move is brilliant, and makes it so there can be dramatic swings in where they are placing each round.  Even when it seems obvious who will win and who will come in last, there is always a chance that a certain die roll will change everything.  The strategy seems a bit elusive for some people, because they don't grasp how and when to make bets (in fact I've yet to be beaten because apparently I get it more than anyone else in my family.)  It's easy to teach but hard to get everyone competitive, which might hold back some people from giving it a chance.  Not the best SdJ winner, but certainly far from the worst.  And that pyramid for rolling the dice is a lot of fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Camel Up is nothing more than one fun silly filler of luck and chance: what makes it such a good game is, there’s little strategy when playing it apart from guessing which camel still has the better chances at placing ahead of the others. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A worthy Spiel des Jahres winner, as it appeals to a broad audience. It's simple enough for families, and is still fun for gamers. In other words, it's a game you can play with your non-gaming friends and not get sick of it when they want to play it over and over.

Shares a genre with Royal Turf / Winner's Circle: racing and betting. If you're familiar with that game, it's like that, except you have much less control over the movement of the racers, but in this one you can make smaller bets during the race, instead of just at the beginning.

I can't decide which I like more -- Royal Turf is painful with a full six-player count and much better with fewer. I like that Camel (C)Up can plays well with large groups. So if I had to pick one game, I'd probably keep Camel (C)Up. I love Royal Turf but there are so many other great games I could play if there are three or four players, and Camel (C)up is the better game for more players.

I've played with 3, 6 and 7 players, all different groups. In two of the games, one player moved the camels significantly more often than other players, and the winner (by a good-size margin) was the player to his or her left. This is because she could pick a bet first after new information was revealed. A potentially serious problem that I'll reconsider after more plays.

But it is a lot of fun. It has visual appeal, is enjoyable by many different types of people, and works well over a large player range. And unlike a lot of games these days, it has real tension and potential for cheers and groans. It's a perfect choice for SdJ.

It's obviously meant to be Camel Cup. I don't care what the back of the box says, the title graphic is clearly intended to convey "Camel Cup" (not nearly as ambiguously as people suggest). Annoys me that they print one thing and claim (retroactively?) it's meant to be something else.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
It handles up to 8.  A racing game where the key is knowing on when to grab bets, when to make the decision if a camel will be in first (or last).  Gambles abound!

RATING: 6
When I first played this game, I loved it! The crazy madness around the odds of every single turn is hilarious.

We're betting on camels on a race where we can, in some degree, influence some events during the race. The mechanism around the last jumps to the top of the stack makes it very hard to predict who's gonna end first on the turn, even tougher to predict who's gonna win the race.

But let's be honest, we (almost) don't have any control of anything that happens in the game. That is fun! Really, it's a fun game, because we never know how things will turn out... I've played games of Camel Up where the last positioned camel on the last turn... wins the race! How can you expect that? The thing is... not to expect anything. Just have fun and laugh! 

Now that I've played it so many times, I don't love it. I don't know if I still like or not. I'll keep it as a 7, but this the type of game (now) where I get pissed off more often than I enjoy it. The luck plays such a major part in this game that it drains the fun of it. What used to be fun, now gets me mad.

All in all, it's a good game. It lasted in my good graces for long time. Now I can't even play it. I'll stick with the memories! ;)

RATING: 7
Initally very surprised at how much fun I had playing this game - and surprised at how much fun I've had with the game at a table full of adults too. The game creates a genuinely exciting atmosphere and always generates a lot of laughter and friendly indignation. It's not a particularly deep game strategically, but it's certainly a fantastically executed roll-and-move game - never devolves into a frustrating experience for players who continually get "bad rolls" as their bad luck can be mitigated (or hilariously exacerbated) by the bets they place. Roll-and-move done right and always good fun - only rated 7/10 as, despite how well I think the game is exectued,  I do have to be in the right mood to play games like this.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
Racing and betting game where players can choose to roll dice, place bets or put down tiles in hopes of having the camels they bet on win the leg (which ends after each camel rolls the die ones) or the race (when one camel crosses the finish line.)

Recognizable because of the stacking camels; camels that land on another will pile up, the topmost camel is the one in the lead--and camels that move will carry those that are on top along for the ride.

RATING: 5
A decently fun betting/wagering game, where you bet on the outcome of a camel race.

The novelty here is a pyramid which dispenses the dice.  The order in which the dice come out highly affects the outcome of each stage of the race, so while you can play the odds, your bets will get shot in the foot very often.

I didn't love it, and I didn't hate it.  Not a game I'd suggest playing, but if someone else wants to play, I wouldn't refuse.

RATING: 8
Feels like another version of Manila. Your control in the game is how you bet, not how the racers perform. The tension is on when you bet, the earlier you bet, the greater the reward, but the greater the likelihood of being wrong. So you want to bet just before everyone else does, but if you wait too long the gamble is a sure thing and everyone else has already placed their bets and you get nothing.

It's also a game that feels silly, so no one looks at you funny when you call out stuff like, Go Green Go!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a terrific little betting/racing filler/family game. I love that the camels start in different spots at the beginning of the race and for each leg, and of course that they stack - this creates different positions and unique betting situations each round. 

I also think the game creates fun tension between the short-term and long-term betting, and invites risk-taking with the payout structures. Another key to the game working are the +1/-1 tiles you can use to subtly influence the outcome of the race. Whenever you make a bet, you have to consider how following players can screw you with the tiles. It adds a good deal of richness to the betting. 

It's just a lot of little details that make for a fresh-feeling, fun game. Everything sets up and plays in 20-30 minutes - very nice game. A worthy winner for game of the year.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I think this game proves that having one or two clever mechanisms can really elevate a game that otherwise would feel like "been there, done that." Such is the case with last year's SdJ winner.

The pyramid represents a twist on the classic dice tower, and knowing that by choosing to roll you are giving valuable information to other players is truly agonizing. Add to that the uncertainty of when to place bets on the winner and the loser to maximize your take in the long game, and you see that Camel Up offers real choices and isn't totally random.

I liked this game but I didn't love it - it's the kind of game where I'd happily play if asked, but I doubt I'd request it. It also solidified my thought that Splendor should have won the SdJ!

RATING: 4
Art:  10
Uniqueness: 10
Concept: 9
Mechanics: 3
Overall game: 4

Technically, I never owned this game, but I wanted to add to to my list so I remind myself not to buy it.  

Here's what's awesome:  The game looks excellent, the idea of stacking camels and planning ahead is cool, the pyramid with the dice mechanism is fun.  

Here's the problem with this game:  It makes you feel like you have some strategy to control it, but really, all that matters is the last 10 spaces.  The whole early part of the of the game is wasted time and energy.   I kept yearning to have more control to effect the outcome, but it wasn't there.  Also, it hurt my head a little.  A little more brain power was needed than I wanted to to give.  

If pushed, I will try playing it again.  Maybe with practice I can iron out my concerns.

RATING: 10
Handling up to 8 (10 with the expansion), this is my go-to pick for large groups of casual or mixed gamers. With only 4 available actions, it's easy to explain and plays quickly, even with a full table. The actions offer a nice balance between surety and uncertainty, leading to some interesting choices and rewarding outcomes. The wacky movement of the camels almost always engenders favorites and underdogs, leading players to cheer when "their" camel makes an unexpected move or groan as a pack leader inexplicably finishes a leg in last place. This game has generated more group cheering and stand-up die rolls than any other in my collection. 

My most-played game at the Gathering of Friends 2014.

Still fun with the right people, good intro game, but looses its luster quickly.

[July 2015 - 7.4]
I might have rated Camel Up a little higher after my first play or two, but after some more plays, there are some issues -- mainly dependent on who you play with. 

It's a great family/party game and easy to learn, but I almost find playing with gamers more enjoyable. 

The key for more fun, in my opinion, is having people place bets earlier rather than later. This leads to more investment and emotion, as you pull for, and try to change the outcome (with the +1/-1 tiles). Otherwise (and this is what I find with some newer players) people just play it safe and just roll and roll. When this happens, the game turns into one of more complete luck dependent of where you are in the turn order -- there's really no time for any sort of strategy or fun.

Still, play with the right people, make some crazy bets and this can be a rousing good time. I love to see the last-place camel come back for the win.

RATING: 7
Light-hearted family-weight racing game that doesn't wear out its welcome.   It's sort of like a simplified hybrid of Winner's Circle and Russelbande.  The presentation is excellent.   There's a bare minimum of control or meaningful choice.   The movement system allows for camels in the back to catch up if the dice come out of the pyramid in the right order.   That's the most interesting element to keep track of.   Plays a large group well, and there are a lot of swing-y moments which make the game fun if played in the right mindset.  Can be played in 20-30 minutes.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
2014 Spiel des Jahres Winner.  Light family style game, plays quickly, easy to learn, and fun.  

Played a four-player game twice.  Can be very volatile with positions changing quickly, which makes it hard to bet correctly, but also keeps it fun.  Feels somewhat random, but less so than some think.  Timing of bets is important, and seizing opportunities to bet when you think a camel is likely to win - this is the heart of the game (not trying to make a particular camel win, which is nearly impossible!).  Realize that taking pyramid action does often help your opponents by giving them more info.

Great comment from deedob [url=https://www.boardgamegeek.com/listitem/4143416?commentid=5754624#comment5754624]here[/url]:
[q]A very misunderstood game.

I found that there are two type of players for Camel (C)up:
1) Those that bet early and hope for the best while avoiding the pyramid action since it "gives your opponent information you don't benefit from".
2) Those that wait and try to time their actions to make bets with the most possible returns for their actions and are not afraid to take the pyramid action once in a while.

Players of type 1 always think this game is all "random and no strategy" and ultimately don't think this game is fun.
Players of type 2 thinks there's much more than luck involved and have a great time.

However, players of type 2 tend to win the game almost all the time, thus proving that the "no strategy and all random" part is completely wrong.[/q]

lacxox adds:
[q]this game is not about influencing the outcome of the race (hey, when can you influence real races you made real bets on anyway?) but on betting and grabbng the best opportunities at the best time.[/q]

RATING: 6
A fun betting game where you try to make some money between multiple legs of a race. Hedging bets on which camel will come in first and last place, and which camels will be in the first or second position at the end of each leg of the race. It's fun being able to place oasis tokens in such a way that they can help spring some of the lagging camels up ahead of the pack, or to cause the leading camels to fall behind to the bottom of a leading stack. It can really throw off the order of things, which keeps the guessing game interesting from start to finish.

RATING: 5
Well. I guess I can see why the jury chose Camel Up as the Spiel des Jahres. It's quite easy to grasp, plays quickly, and - with people in the right mood anyway - will easily ellicit some cheering and Schadenfreude. Those are nice qualities for a family game.

However, the actual game here is really thin. Betting on the camels comes down to simple probability calculations, and since there is almost no way to actually influence the race results, that's pretty much all there is to it.

RATING: 6
For some quick dice-driven luck, I haven't experienced a game this fun since Manila. Camel Up is not going to blow your mind. It is not going to make you think. But, by letting go of pretensions, I have seen tables shouting with joy and groaning in dismay, which is a pretty fantastic feat for a game about camel meeples being pushed around a square space. 

What makes the game? The "dice pyramid"! There's something about seeing the dice pop out of that pyramid that is so much more exciting than just chucking dice.

Update: I dropped the score after being over-exposed to this one. The game's betting mechanic offers diminishing returns but I'll still play it once in a while if requested.

RATING: 8
The strategy of this game is much more elusive than you would expect from a game that is, basically, for kids. I had to play a few games to get the nuance of the strategy and another few to get good at it, but thankfully it's a quick game.  

You're essentially bidding on probabilities, and the game richly rewards the player who bids first but still mildly penalizes incorrect guesses, so you have to weigh when to bid on camels along the spectrum of "possible winner" to "sure bet", knowing full well that the situation can change drastically with just one die roll. There is some luck involved, but a good player will still win most of the time.

RATING: 8
Once upon a time I went on a long journey on a camel.  T'was indeed a bumpy ride.  I tell the long version every time we pull Camel Up from the shelf.  This has no bearing on my opinion of the game but why break a habit?  Camel Up is nothing if not entertaining.  A race can take as little as 15 mins, we never play just once, and there are always cheers and boos as the winning camel crosses the line.  It is colourful, witty (a touch whacky, even)and fun.  And when I swear never to tell my tale again I can look forward to hearing the long suffering groans as I happily break my promise.  I love meta-gaming.

RATING: 6
First off, the font clearly states Camel Cup.  Otherwise the capitol "c" would extend above the lowercase "a" and not down past the bottom of the "u".  Also, if the second word was "up", the "u" would be bigger than the "p".  Secondly, there is the exact same probability of 1, 2, or 3. . . This means there is little to no strategy to, well, anything.  I see no reason to not bet on the real ponies if this is your thing.  At least you could wave your winnings around instead of gloating that "My 33% came up and yours didn't."  I could see this being a really good game if all the dice had different probabilities or there were more ways to make long vs short term decisions.

RATING: 5.5
Very light race betting game. The movement mechanic, which includes stacking wooden camels, is quite original, but also very random and abstract. Having camels racing in Egypt sets the game apart from the more usual horse races and gives room for a gimmicky pyramid to roll dice. Not only the values rolled are important, but also the order in which the dice come out. Since you can, on your turn, either roll a die or bet, this creates a situation where you don't want to roll, because it gives more information to the other players. There are some tactical decisions, but luck obviously plays a big role.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Tétova tevefutam
Kellemes szórakozást ígérő versenyfutam 2-8 játékos részére, szuper autók helyett itt kétpúpú tevékkel versenyezve. Játékosaink messzi földről érkezett vagy helyi fogadók (hölgyek és urak vegyesen), akik megpróbálják a szerencsét saját javukra állítva a legtöbb pénzt megszerezni a futam végig.
A játék javára írható, hogy több játékos esetében is arányaiban rövid a játékidő, könnyen tanulhatóak a szabályok (amely magyarul is elérhető). A magas szerencsefaktort vagy tudja valaki tolerálni, vagy nem. Természetesen a játék vége felé már jobban látszik, hogy melyik púpos hoz több pénzt a konyhára, akár az első helyre várjuk, akár az utolsóra, de addig a szerencsésebb kezűek már fogadtak arra a „paripára”. Bár azt még maga Allah sem tudja megmondani, hogy az első pár szakasz tevéi közül ki keveredik ki győztesen a homokfújta sivatagi pálya káoszából a célszalagnál, átvágva a délibábok és oázisok mezői között. De talán ilyen lehet egy igaz arab futam, egyre fokozódó hangzavar, szitkozódás, imádság, izzadás, majd a végén pénzzel teli csillogó szemű nyertesek és újabb futamot kérő vesztesek.
Na ennek megfelelően vagy a te játékod, vagy nem. Nekem tetszik.
Megjegyzés: több játékosnál egy-két szerencsés fogadás már a győzelemhez vezet, azonban kevesebb személynél már több jó fogadás szükséges ehhez.

Fun gambling game and plays 2-8

On your turn pick a camel to win. If your camel wins you get X amount of coins at the end of that league. If you pick a tile which allows you to roll a die collect 1 coin at the end of the league.

FUNNEST part of this game is that camels can stack on top of each other and when the camel below moves, all camels stacked on top of it moves too !

RATING: 3
http://jemmagazin.hu/camelup/
"A Camel Upban egy dolgot lehet tenni: reménykedni. A játékosoknak szinte semmilyen ráhatásuk nincsen magára a versenyre és annak eredményére, leszámítva a sivatag/
oázisjelölőket, amelyek, még ha minimálisan is, de befolyásolni tudják a verseny menetét. A verseny már a kezdetektől egészen a végéig a kockákon múlik, hiszen már a tevék kezdő pozícióját is azokkal dobjuk ki, az egymás nyakába mászó tevék szinte teljes káoszban rohannak a cél felé, bármilyen kidolgozott stratégia teljesen felesleges.
Az egyetlen lépés, amivel hozzátehetünk a játékhoz az, amikor az egyik tevét léptetjük, de ezzel sem magunknak segítünk, hanem a többi játékosnak, hiszen a lépés után (főleg az utolsó előtti teve lépésénél) már látszani fog, hogy melyik teve biztosan nem fog nyerni, és melyik tevéknek van még esélyük a nyerésre – viszont ekkorra már általában elfogynak a szavazólapok.
A Camel up egy viccesen kaotikus játék, amit egy másodpercig sem szabad komolyan venni. Kisebb gyerekekkel
ideális játék, hiszen a szerencsén kívül szinte semmi más
nem számít, és minél többen játsszuk, annál jobb." 
De komolyabb játékosok kerüljék el messziről.

RATING: 7.9
起始每人3元
四個動作可以做:
A.拿取當回合下注板塊
B.放置沙漠板塊賽道、或更改沙漠板塊位置(可以換面放不可以原地翻面)(需要間隔至少一格)，被踩到一次得一元。
C.拿取1塊錢金字塔收入板塊，並且搖一顆骰子出來。
D.放置最終名次卡，猜測第一名與最後一名，一次只能下一邊一張
 移動方式:
1.有背一起走
2.往前疊上去，往後背其他人。

RATING: 6.9
Light betting/speculation game. Players are placing bets each round on the positions in the race of the different camels. Each round, each camel will move once (when its die is randomly rolled), but the tricky thing is if there are other camels on top of the camel that is moving, they all advance! So things can get a bit silly and change very quickly.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
A race game where the players bet on races which they can influence indirectly.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
There's only so much game you can squeeze out of a racing theme, after all how many tactics are there in going as fast as possible? Here the emphasis is very much on betting as the camels move in a random sequence, but you can bet on overall winners and losers as well as first and second places over each leg. The only weak point is that you don't actually want to move a camel as that gives more information to the next player, and your reward? A scant $1. So a high luck factor, but often uproariously funny as the most obvious winners get landed on by those behind. This is plain and simply fun and the best race game since Snow Tails.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.1
Bokkensprong 15/04/'16 met Noor, Pepijn, Pieter, Ruthje en ik. Toegankelijk familiespel waarbij je moet gokken welke van vijf gekleurde kamelen de etappe/de hele race zal winnen/verliezen. In je beurt doe je één van vier acties: 1) een kameel evenveel stappen verplaatsen als de dobbelsteen met de overeenkomstige kleur (komt uit piramide). Kamelen die reeds op deze kameel staan, verplaatsen mee; 2) een etappekaart nemen in de kleur van de kameel waarvan je denkt dat die de etappe zal winnen (levert 5, 3, 2 ptn op als je juist gokt, of -1 als je fout gokt); 3) één van je vijf eigen racekaarten leggen bij de kameel waarvan je denkt dat die de eindrace zal winnen of verliezen (kan van 8 tot -1 ptn opleveren); 4) een woestijntegel op de racebaan leggen die ptn oplevert als er een kameel op eindigt, en die die vervolgens een plaats naar voren of naar achteren stuurt. Leuk familiespel.

RATING: 7
Camel Up is a fun race betting game that can be enjoyed by everybody - children and adults, gamers and non-gamers. It's very quick to teach and evokes a lot of excitement with the right group as you cheer on the camels hoping for good (or bad) dice rolls.  Very dynamic, very interactive, very light, and all fun for it.  The one element that hardcore gamers must be ready to accept is less deterministic game play.  There are times the player can bet on safe odds, but overall the dice make luck as key as strategy.  But isn't that the point of race betting, anyway?

RATING: 3
2015-07-12

Initial Rating: 3.0 (July 2015)

As 2014 Spiel des Jahres Winner I was extremely wary about Camel Up! The games they choose are almost always disliked by me. I tried to stay far away from it but a friend dragged me into a game.  As it turned out I was correct, I heavily dislike Camel Up! 

The game is almost pure luck AND it is too long for the level of luck (the game isn’t that long, what I’m saying is that game duration Vs. the luck factor doesn’t fit with my gaming interests). It has obvious decisions and/or uninformed decisions, the game situation can change radically from one turn to the next so you have very little room to plan, pure chaos.

I heavily dislike racing themes.

On the good side, the game components are very good, the pyramid is gorgeous and clever and the art is great too.

Bottom line, Camel Up! can be fun (if played with the correct game group), however I feel I wasted my precious gaming time playing it. I think it can be a great family game geared toward children but it is way too light for me. Almost pure luck. I won’t ever play it again.

Current Rating: 3.0

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.1
This was one I really enjoyed. The two best parts, the camels can stack on one another and there's a "dice-pyramid" which allows for one die to be rolled at a time to move the camels. On a player's turn, they can do one of four things: One, roll a die with the pyramid to move a camel or a group of camels (like I said, camels stack so if a camel has camels on top of it and it needs to move, it carries the other camels with it. Two, place a desert or oasis tile on the board that can either help or hurt a camel by allowing it to move ahead one extra space or move back one. Three, place a bet on which camel they think will be in the lead during one leg of the race. And four, place a bet on which camels they think will either win the race or lose the race. Excellent and fun game with a lot of variety. I would like to try this one out with the full compliment of eight people sometime in the future.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
5+ plays

Camel Up (or is it Cup?) is a great game when you consider its goal to bring more people into tabletop games.  We trade high chance and limited options in order to gain accessibility, simple mechanics, and the chance to get a wider audience to play games that actually engage the brain.

There is a nice balance of risky bets and conservative plays, and plenty of options: players can choose to move the race along or instead rig the race or place bets before others. Players with a head for probabilities will find something to dig in to while playing casually is just as enjoyable.

Camel Up's short length (15-30 minutes) means more variance and less skill, but makes it easy to bring in new players and play multiple games.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
In Camel Up, up to eight players bet on five racing camels, trying to suss out which will place first and second in a quick race around a pyramid. The earlier you place your bet, the more you can win — should you guess correctly, of course. Camels don't run neatly, however, sometimes landing on top of another one and being carried toward the finish line. Who's going to run when? That all depends on how the dice come out of the pyramid dice shaker, which releases one die at a time when players pause from their bets long enough to see who's actually moving!

RATING: 8
I really enjoyed this game. I was hyped to play it, and I think it did its job really well and lived up to the hype. It's not super competitive, but it's competitive enough to keep people drawn to the game. Oh, and it's a game that doesn't suffer from Munchkinitis, which is a great achievement. The luck aspect (its reliance on dice rolls) isn't actually a deterrence in this game, because it's not going to be that game that carries the party: that's reserved for more resource-intensive games like Puerto Rico, Le Havre, and Agricola/Caverna. This game is just cool because it's a solid time-waster that keeps the hardcore gamers occupied with strategy, and the casual gamers enticed by easy rules and an element of randomness so that you're never truly out of it.

RATING: 10
What an absolute blast this game is.  Quite easy to learn and play, you spend the game making a wager on who will win a leg of the race, who will take first overall in the race and who will place last.  You're not actually playing a camel, but the role of a spectator placing bets on the race.  The game is structured in such a way that it allows for a comeback of a camel in the back of the pack, and as a result, for a player who is losing as well.  I enjoy this aspect in a game (unlike 7 Wonders Duel where if you lost out on a resource in the first round, you've lost out for good).

RATING: 7
Wonderful chaotic game in which you have no control (at all? :-) ). Also, there is a problem with the fact that rolling the die is never really a good idea for the player rolling. Because most of the time it's the next player that will benefit from the roll, since more information is then available. 
But nevertheless, this is a fun game for people that like to gamble. Can be played with children and the whole family. The more people playing, the merrier. 

The camels that stack is a very original feature of this game where you also have to predict who will win.

This game reminds me of [thing=54735][/thing], because it's also a funny unpredictable race where you can bet on who the winner will be.

Minus: 2 - 8 - 10

RATING: 6.75
2-8 Players
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Due to the size of the box you may not realize it, but this is a fantastic filler.  It provides a little bit of luck, some jockeying for position by making smart bets & placing your desert/oasis tile well, and calculating odds, plus it fits perfectly into a 30 minute time slot.

There is luck in the game.  However, it wouldn't be much of a betting game, if it didn't.  You know how the camels are currently positioned, the numbers on the dice, and which dice haven't pulled from the pyramid yet.  This gives you a ton of information on how to bet each leg, but nothing is set in stone.  That's what makes it tense and exciting!

If you hate any sort of luck, stay away from Camel Up.  If you like playing the odds, check it out!

RATING: 6
This is a rough game to categorize. It definitely has it's place. The problem is that when you try to play this game out of it's place, it's really bad. It's not a game to play with any serious tones at all. No one will have fun if anyone is taking the game too seriously. For me, the perfect place for this game is with some kids or people not looking to deep dive into a game at all. In that spot, it works pretty well.

The game does take a bit too long for what it is though. It says 20-30 minutes, and I'd say it's closer to 30 minutes, which is too long. I think 15 minutes would be about perfect for this game.

All in all, it's not a bad game to have in a collection, but I wouldn't say it's a "must have".

RATING: 2

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A stripped down version of Manilla? Well, that's the best comparison I can make anyway. In both games you are betting on an object (camel or punt) to reach the finish line. They both have multiple "legs," in both cases you are not tied to any specific racing object, and of course, in both cases you are gambling. There are several differences though. I'm not a big fan of Manilla with 5. It seems that the board is too tight with 5, and not tight enough with 3. So, I think the sweet spot for Manilla is 4. I've only played Camel Up with 4, but I feel like it would be better with more. 8 might be too many (too long), but I could see 5 or 6 being great! Scalability just seems better in general with Camel Up. I would also argue that it is a better design. However, that doesn't necessarily make me like it better. Another differences that was aforementioned is the fact that this trims the fat of Manilla quite a bit. Of the Spiel contenders this year, I've played Splendor and Camel Up. This one wins by a landslide. 

Update 11/25/14: After 2 more plays (with 4), I've found that it's impossible to calculate simple odds in this game. The possibilities for how camels are stacked and how they more are too complex to identify until most of the dice have come out. Honestly, it's rather chaotic. That said, the best player will still generally win, because that player recognizes when critical opportunities arise. In other words, this game is all about timing. 

Update: I've played it at 4 and 5 players now. It plays really well at both play counts. I actually might like it better at 4. It's already really tight with 5. 5 players becomes more about turn order than timing bets. 

Update 3/21/15: Erin played with the CORE a few nights ago. There were plenty of loud roars and cheers. Everyone had a great time! 

Update 12/29/15: Played this with Donna and Reg tonight. They are FAR from gamers and had a fun tim playing it! This game is so awesome! I'm going to download the iPad app now. I am finally upgrading this to a "9" out of "10."

*FIMO miniature and Egyptian coins

RATING: 9.5
Fantastic game which appeals to both casual and more serious gamers. It's a light game for sure and the luck factor can be crucial but I feel that I can improve my winning chances by making (what I consider) the correct decisions. 
People tend to be either too conservative or too bold with their bets so I think that despite the luck factor, people who better understand the odds will gain some satisfaction by winning more often than the average player.
The game lasts around 20 minutes for us and it's filled with delightful tension and many unexpected and often humorous twists. Usually everyone wants to play again and again and again... Even when I lose badly due to bad luck I don't mind it because the game is always super fun.

RATING: 6
It's pretty good for what it is - a light fun family game. Definitely not something you want to overthink, but if you can just turn your brain off and go with it, it can be a lot of fun. It also plays quickly, which of course is a must for a racing game. 

The one thing I did find mildly annoying is that you can sometimes have an easy and obvious good move fall in your lap when the player before you rolls a die to move a camel, depending of course on which camel moved and what effect it had on the race. That wouldn't be a big deal if it averaged out, but it doesn't, because it only happens a couple/few times during the whole game, so it ends up being sort of a lottery. That's really a minor nit, though. After all, it is a racing game dictated by die rolls, so one has to expect that people will sometimes just get lucky rolls.

RATING: 7.5
Camel Cup ist ein einfaches Familienspiel, zu dem man auch gerne mal einen absoluten Brettspielmuffel einladen kann. Das Spielmaterial ist hübsch und optisch ansprechend, dabei sieht es auch noch einfach total witzig aus. Das bei Camel Cup natürlich Glück einen hohen Stellenwert hat, empfinde ich als nicht weiter schlimm, da es sich so schnell, flott und unkompliziert spielt, dass man auch gerne die eine oder andere Runde mehr spielt.

RATING: 6
Bit of an impulse buy after reading rave reviews. Sounded like a game right up my alley, but a bit disappointed in it. Components are top notch and it's fun to see the camels stack up and watch crazy reversals of fortune. 

However, something about it doesn't click and I think it has to do with the betting. I prefer Longshot which, although longer, captures the feeling of betting on a race a lot better while still managing to be relatively light - I have played Longshot with plenty of nongamers and had fun. 

Camel Up is good, especially if you are looking for a quick filler at 30 minutes or less, but it's made me appreciate Longshot a lot more. 

Played: 5 times.

UPDATE: Taken off of trade because other people really seem to enjoy it as a light filler. I'm still kinda "meh" on it, but keeping it around for that reason.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Camel Up is a racing/betting game where the player with the most money at the end wins. 

Players are able to take one of four actions each turn and they can place bets on legs of the race as well as the final result. 

The two elements that make it unique are the pyramid dice rolling component, which is kind of neat and the fact that camels can stack and in doing so the order of the camels can be altered.

This really is a very light game that is more 'beer & pretzels' than it is anything else.

The game can be exciting at times but the amount of control is quite limited so work out your mileage based on that.  

A game I'm happy to play a few times a year for a laugh with the right group but not one I need to own.

Despite taking longer to play, I still think Long Shot is the better game.

RATING: 9.9
At first glance this may seem to be a racing game, but really it is a betting game, the stakes aren't real and the game is very quick so if you guess poorly and end up out of the running it doesn't sting too much. The stacking camel mechanic is more than just humorous, it makes it deceptively tricky to puzzle out which camel is likely to be left behind and which it likely to take the lead. The artwork it colorful and the pyramid dice-rolling gimmick is the icing on the cake, everyone wants to use that thing and move the camels along. 

If I could only use one word to describe this game it would be [b]F-U-N FUN![/b] So much fun. 

When I played this with for the first time it had exactly that reaction that you would hope for in a game, everyone laughing and joking around, lots of table talk, and then when it was over the unanimous request to [i][b]LET'S PLAY AGAIN[/b][/i]!

RATING: 8
Camel Up somehow manages to do a fantastic job of simulating a the feeling of a day at the (strangely Camel-based) races. There's a nice blend of luck vs. logic to this one and it's amazingly easy to see how it won so many awards. The whole game revolves around betting on which camel is most likely to win each segment of the race, however early bids have better odds and leaving it too late can really hurt your winnings.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a light family game that won the 2014 Spiel des Jahres. There are five different colored camels that are racing around a board. The race consists of a few legs, with payouts given to the winner of each leg and the game ends when one camel crosses the finish line. Players have 4 choices on their turn: get a bet token for payout on a leg, roll a die, bet on overall winner or loser, or place their oasis token (which when a camel lands on, can move it +1 or -1 spot).

It's quite unpredictable until the end, and it is fun.  The more players there are, the less control there is, so just enjoy the ride. There is a lot of luck, but the game is actually enjoyable. There is a lot of groaning, laughing and making fun of other people's bets. My rating is more about the experience and fun, not for the skill involved. I haven't tried this game with 7 or 8 players yet. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
A dice-driven racing game in which betting for current leader occurs each turn, and each turn consists of one die roll for each camel. The twist (and name of the game) comes from the fact that camels stack and carry one another by landing on the same space. It reminds me of Top Race, but this one's a better game. Since it's fun and supports up to 8, I can see this one hitting the table a lot.

It's clear why this game won the SdJ, and it's also clear that the SdJ ain't the same award that Settlers received.

RATING: 6.5
I initially despised Camel Up as a totally random/lucky game. After playing it, it certainly is a lucky game, but you still have some actions available that can affect the outcome in a small way. You still won't win if you're not lucky enough, but the game lasts only 30 minutes and it has some fun moments.

The components are OK. The pyramid replaces the usual cloth bag only to make the game more eye-catching, but it doesn't work that well. The art is quite good.

I would not recommend it to more than 6 players. It is just too random, you take very few actions.

So, it's a nice light short game that accommodates many players, but it's far from being the best family game of the year (Spiel des Jahres).

RATING: 8
[b]Camel Up[/b] was sold via the marketplace 1/30/18.
Received in a math trade (3/17/15)

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]Camel Up has easily become my favorite game played a year ago and my pick for family game of the year for games new to me in 2015. This game has been a hit with everyone we;ve introduced it to, it is a great family/gateway/party game. While not the most serious or strategic game it gets rowdy. I can't recommend this game highly enough for 4+ players, it has become a go to game when we have friends and family over. You can teach this game in about two minutes and then you're off. I am actually surprised at how much we enjoy this game and didn't think it would have the staying power it does, but it continues to get pulled off the shelf.[/i] 

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- Awesome family/party game that can be taught to anyone in minutes.
- Components are top notch, the camel meeples are awesome!
- Fun... really fun. [i](Seriously; this game is a blast to play, trust me!)[/i]
- There is just enough happening with the camels (due to the stacking mechanism) to keep this game engaging and unpredictable, which makes each turn exciting.

After playing a few times I believe Camel Up definitely deserved to win the Spiel award. This is a game that you really have to play, reading about it will not get across just how much fun this game can be. This is not a serious game by any means and should not be judged as such. It is a gambling game with a lot of luck involved, but you will be cheering and groaning as the camels you bet on go from first to last on the final leg of a race! I highly recommend this game to anyone looking for a great game you can play with anyone.[/i]

RATING: 7
心得:
熱鬧的賭博賽跑遊戲
規則簡單
主要是賽跑結果容易峰迴路轉
設計得很好
規則:
*最年輕玩家當起始，投擲五顆骰子決定駱駝起始位置，數字一樣疊起來，由起始玩家決定怎麼疊
*每個玩家拿三元加一個顏色的下注卡跟沙漠圖板
*玩家可選行動如下
1.拿一片回合賭注板塊
2.放置你的沙漠板塊在賽道上或者移動已經在賽道上自己的沙漠板塊
(賽道第一格不能擺放，只能擺在沒駱駝的位置，沙漠板塊不能相鄰)
3.拿一片金字塔板塊並拿起場上的金字塔擲骰(分段賽結束有一元)
4.使用一張牌預測最後的贏家以及輸家
(覆蓋在輸贏預測區，一旦預測順序就不能更動
可以每回合出一張不同色的牌重複預測)
*分段賽結束沙漠板塊回手，根據賭注板塊金字塔板塊拿錢
*當第一隻駱駝衝過終點線遊戲結束，最後一次分段賽開獎，跟進行總冠軍吊車尾開獎
*駱駝前進時(帶著上面的)該格有其他駱駝會疊在上面，後退的話該格駱駝會在最上面

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Takes the old Russelbande piggyback movement system (which is an excellent and fun mechanic) and jazzes it into a non-kid's game by adding various forms of betting to the game. Betting isn't my favourite genre - I've ditched Manila previously - so this has upside and downside. There's no hidden information, you're just making decisions based on the odds, and to reap the big bucks you need to make decisions on what to bet on before the odds are in your favour. Which makes it a so-so guessing game really, but at least the game goes fast and provides some cheer/groan factor as the movement dice are finally revealed. I can see why it might be popular but it's nothing more than an occasional outing for me.

RATING: 5
Okay, this one was just silly. You're betting on a bunch of camels involved in a race, but the camels pretty much move randomly. Camels that land on the same space as other camels actually land on top of them, and are considered ahead. Furthermore, if a camel with another camel on top moves, the one on top moves with it. You get money by betting on each "leg" (a round of each camel moving once) and on the winner and loser of the entire race. The game featured chunky stackable wooden camels and an elaborate pyramid-shaped dice cup that concealed not only the distance the camel would move but also the identity of the camel that would move. These gimmicks made the game feel very silly, but really, there wasn't much game here.

RATING: 8

Just approach this in a party game mood and fun is guaranteed.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Camel Up (not to be confused with Camel Cup, a game that does not exist) is a betting racing game with camels. There are five camels of five colors, corresponding to five dice with 1-3 on them that are placed inside a convoluted pyramid to be randomly generated. Each round, or leg, of the race, you can choose to grab bet tiles (which earn you money if the camel you choose is in the lead (or one buck if it's in second), make a bet on the first or last place at the end of the race, or advance the race by producing one of the five dice (which will also reward you with a camelbuck at the end of the leg), or place a desert or oasis that if landed on gives you a buck and moves the landing camel(s) forward or back. When camels move into the same space as another camel, the stack UP on it, and if the bottom camel moves, it carries those above it. At the end of each leg you score your bets, and as soon as a camel crosses the finish, you score the race bets.

Overall, the game has some interesting nuances to interact with a random number/camel generator, producing odd movement as a camel moves forward, climbs onto another camel and then rides that one forward (possibly repeating this process with rapidly stacking camels). The physical design of the game is really great, everything is made of tile or cards just how it should be, and the board space is used just right. The pyramid die generator is I'd say sorta gimmicky, it does something a bag could do in a somewhat convoluted fashion. I crushed it quite impressively with 43 bucks, with second place only have 27, and the game plays quite quickly.

It does the whole 'race/bet' premise fairly nicely, and its mechanics are quite clever, but I'm not sure they're clever or interesting enough to truly be that great. I understand it won quite a few awards, which makes sense, but at the same time those awards are indicative of pretty middle of the road products. I'm curious about Supercup when it's completed.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

RATING: 6

Any game that can engender such feelings is doing pretty good at making for a fun and memorable time.

RATING: 5.5
2015-03-14: For a game to play with my 6/7-year-old niece and nephews, an 8! This is one fiddly racing game that my niece and nephews quite enjoyed! Although they probably can't comprehend the strategy or tactics in the game, they are still enjoying it. I don't think they understood the point of the desert tiles (and so they ignored them -- or placed them way too far ahead of track). They did understand the idea that no one owned a camel but they were betting on which one to win (even though at the beginning of the game they wanted to own one of the camels).

One plus though is how quick the games are. With kids, you tend to play the same games over and over and over again.

I suppose I would rate this a 3 if I were to play it with my regular gaming group, though, because of the total lack of control in the game.

I couldn't imaging playing this with more than four players.

UPDATE: After playing this one about 8 more times with my niece, this game will be a personal favourite of mine as I think this is probably the first "strategy" game in which my niece figured out the strategy all by herself!

RATING: 7
Pros:
1. Mix of Luck and Strategy. This game has a great mix of luck and strategy. You can play trying to maximize probabilities, but the dice might still get you. This makes it a great family game that kids can play with adults and still win.
2. Pyramid. The pyramid dice roller that comes with this game is excellent. Fun to just play with.
3. Easy to teach. This game takes less than 5 minutes to teach.

Summary: I don't have any cons to this game. It's an all around solid game. There's nothing that jumps out at you when you're playing. You don't feel like you've accomplished anything when you win. There's a little excitement in watching the race play out. But overall, I doubt I'd ever play this game again unless it is with children. That's not a bad thing, but it does result in a lower overall score for me.

RATING: 7
Amazing little game of luck and gambling. You're betting on the camels, but situation can change in the blink of an eye. Not entirelly mindless, you have to be good at estimating probabilities, but in the end, you'll be on the mercy of the dice gods. Which is very fine in a game like this!

Great gateway, great beer and pretzels game, fast and crazy in a very positive way. Is it worthy of the Spiel des Jahres title? =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.224
2P to 8P game.

It's a 5 camel race of one lap around the track.  The race is divided into several betting sessions called 'legs'....a leg is when each camel rolls the die once.  If a camel lands on another, then he stacks on top....if the bottom camel moves, everyone on top moves with him.  So you bet on which camel will be ahead at the end of the current leg.  You can also make a longer term bet (with a bigger payout) on what camel you think will win the entire race....early bets have a bigger payout, but are more likely to be wrong as the race is very dynamic and can change very quickly.

Highly recommended for a light, quick, 'laugh-at-the-result' type game.  If you want to employ a superior strategy to dominate your opponents, look elsewhere. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game was much more fun than I thought it would be.  When a group of 30+ year old guys start giggling like school kids throughout the game you know it's a good time.

There is a lot of randomness in the game.  I tend to shy away from random games.  Just be sure not to expect a great deal of solid strategy.  If you are willing to roll with the swings and just enjoy the concept for what it is, you'll have a lot of fun.

RATING: 8.5
Light hearted betting game. You can quite easily calculate the different probabilities for the short-horizon bets, so there is not so much to the game if played seriously. But for casual play, maybe even with children who do not recognize the proabilities so easily, this is quite some fun. The pyramid-dice-rolling mechanism is totally overproduced, but it is a nice gimmick which makes Camel Up very recognizable.

Update: Played it also with many players (7) and it still worked great. Very easy to teach, great components, good artwork, always fun: I think I like this game more than I should based on the mechanisms. 6.5 -> 7

Update 2: After more than 10 plays with different groups (also many non-gamers) I have to increase my rating once more. Camel Up! is just a extremely well designed and fun family game. The central mechanisms with the dice rolls and the stacking camels offers such different outcomes of the race, such that most of the times the result (even of a single leg) cannot be predicted with certainty. 7 -> 7.5

Update 3: After more than 20 plays, I still enjoy every single one of them. Camel up scales really well over a wide range of number of players. This is one of the best family games. It's really unique. 7.5->8

Update 4: After 25 play and with the expansion being released, Camel Up! receives another bump. Best game of 2014 for me. Worthy Spiel des Jahres winner.

RATING: 5
07-10-2014. Rated after 3 plays apparently. Simple bidding game, with nice components. Game won "Spiel des Jahres 2014" so I wanted to try it out. 

Camel Up is a fluffy bidding game. Each camel races around the track -over several rounds- and you bet on which comes over the finish first and which is ahead at the end of the round. Thing is, camels on the same spot are stacked and camels on top of the one being moved are moved with it.

It's not bad, but I couldn't really care for it.

RATING: 6
Brilliant little family game with a whimsical theme and a bit more strategy than some are admitting. The camel-stacking adds a surprising amount to the decision space. Given what the award has evolved into, I rate this a near perfect choice for SdJ.
Despite all the whimsy, this is NOT a game for younger kids. An understanding of basic probability is required, or there becomes a seat-order binding issue, where the person sitting to the left of the kid will win. I would argue this is a game for at least ages 10+.

RATING: 8
This game admittedly looks ridiculous, but it's a box full of fun. The rules are well-written and straight-forward, and the premise of the game is nice and simple: place bets on a wacky camel race, and periodically cash in (or pay out) on your bets. Most money at the end wins. 

Played this with 4 players and things worked well. I'm interested to know how the strategy changes with more or fewer players. 

The pyramid die roller seems gimmicky but it really adds to the excitement. A lot of die rolls near the end had everyone's head near the table trying to see what was coming out. 

The game is pretty balanced in that no one ever really seems out of it -- both the camels racing and the players playing. Does white look assured of last place? Not so fast, a couple of lucky rolls later and white is pushing for the win.

The game is the right length, enough that it's easy to play twice in a row without anyone getting tired of it.

Happy to have this one in my collection.

RATING: 6
I didn't expect this winning SdJ, but was relieved it wasn't the soulless Splendour. I didn't know what to expect, but the game pleasantly surprised me. We organised a boardgame section at a local sci-fi+fantasy convention and this game was a big hit. Looking pleasant, being easy to play, but mostly evoking a fun atmosphere. 

It's racing betting game (betting on camels) with a new gimmick of camels stacking on top of one another. While dice introduce the usual randomness (d3, btw.), it's the tiles and aggressive play of them that really turns the chaos button on. With the race being divided in legs (where each camel moves once) the game is all about timing, trying to prioritise short and long term goals and trying to detect when the tide will turn before anybody else does. I actually loved this riding on the groupthink and saying  [i]"ha, I knew this was going to happen"[/i] afterwards (of course, I predicted also other things, that didn't happen, but I get results!). 

What the game does really well is exuding a pleasant and exciting atmosphere full of laughs and some [i]"A-Ha!"[/i]s. Art is pretty much the usual somewhat cute somewhat generic German family game fare. Pyramid - yes, it's gimmicky, but actually clever in how it does help the game go along faster and smoother, so good job on user interface. Maybe the tricky part is that it's kinda gamerish - you do need to think and have plans and adapt them all the time, but you have no certainty that your planning will be rewarded. However having no plans won't win you the game either - I'm not sure if its simple enough to get that I could play it with kids. 

Now, they tell me, Winner's Circle (of which I believe there isn't a copy in the country) is a better racing betting game. I can't tell. Certainly is better than the other one I've played (Horse Fever - good core, but bad execution). It also doesn't seem like a game people will play years from now. Yet, the game allows me to use my skills of prediction and I love that. Not sure if many other games do this (?).

RATING: 5
The first thing that comes to mind about Camel Up is that it is one overproduced game. The pyramid and pyramid tiles are totally unnecessary, but there is no denying that the set-up commands curiosity. 

Kitschy visuals aside, the stacking of camels is an interesting gimmick which can lead to hilarious upsets. There are a few meaningful decisions to be made while betting, but otherwise the gameplay teeters close to complete chaos. Not only does the value of each roll matter, but the order in which dice are revealed also counts just as much.

Something worth noting is that the decisions can occasionally feel constricted. When at least 2 dice have been rolled in an early leg, the next player will often have to decide between rolling a die or taking a betting card. Neither option is attractive because taking a betting card would be highly risky with 3 unrolled dice remaining, and rolling a die would significantly reduce the betting risks for subsequent players. If everyone at the table is playing with even a modicum of strategy, this would be an unenviable position to be in.

But there are times you want to turn your brain off and enjoy a cute gimmick in a short amount of time. Camel Up certainly fits that bill, although there are better and more substantial racing games of the same weight out there.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
1 play, 4er

This is a simple (camel-) racing, betting game. The race track is a simple ring around the board. There are 5 colored camels, with a like-colored die hidden in the over-produced (but very cool) pyramid. There's a pile of betting tiles (5, 3, 1) for each camel. Players start the game with some money coins, a +1/-1 token, and a card corresponding to each camel.

On your turn, either take a betting tile, place one of your cards on the first-place or last-place pile, place your +1/-1 token on the track (not adjacent to another such tile), or take a random die from the pyramid and roll -- that camel moves as many spaces forward (if landing on a +/-1 move +/-1 space, and that tile's owner earns 1 coin). Camels moving forward onto another space stack on top of other camels; moving backwards go underneath. After all 5 camels have moved, players earn (or pay!) money according to the positions of the camels they took betting tiles for. Then, return all betting tiles and repeat.

The game ends when a camel crosses the finish line. Then, reveal all cards on the first- and last- place piles. Players who correctly predicted first/last place earn (or pay) additional money; earlier betters get paid better. The player with the most money wins.

So how was it? Lame. There is so little control that the game feels almost totally random. It's not completely random, of course; and it was sort of fun. But there are just so many better racing games out there!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I was looking for a fun (not just heads-down, deep-thinking), relatively short (30-45 minutes), interactive, simple game for up to eight players and came across Camel Up. After playing for the third time in one evening with our gaming cohorts, my wife said, "This is the most fun we've had with any game we've played in quite a while!" And I completely agree. It is witty, it is exciting, it is strategic, it is filled with luck, and it's a blast. 

There are five camels racing around the track. Each player is a bettor. One of four actions can be taken each turn: roll a die to move a camel, bet on the winner of that leg, place your oasis/mirage tile, or bet on the overall race winner/loser. That's it...but there is oh, so much more! This is my favorite aspect of the entire game: if a camel lands on the space of another camel, the moving camel is stacked on top of the other and is then higher ranked than the first. If the camel at the bottom of a stack is moved, all camels on top of that camel move with it and remain ahead of the moving camel. If you think about it, there is a lot that this implies. It muddies up the relatively simple betting world and adds an incredibly fun twist. If a camel lands on an oasis tile, the player who laid the tile gets an Egyptian Pound (have the most at the end of the game to win), and the camel moves forward one space (and takes the lead if stacked). However, a mirage tile will move the camel back a space and underneath any existing camels. Use these tiles carefully to pull in a good stream of earnings while furthering or hindering camels depending on your bets.  

Another really cool feature of Camel Up is the die-rolling pyramid. You put all five dice inside this pyramid at the beginning of each leg. When a player chooses to move a camel for his action, he takes the pyramid, gives it a little shake, flips it upside down, pushes the slider which only allows space enough for a single die to be released, then lifts it up to reveal the die. My 10-year-old nephew rolled almost every time because he thought it was so fun just to use the pyramid.   

The most fun comes when all eggs are placed in one basket, someone flips over the pyramid to roll a die, everyone is muttering something like, "Come on...come on...yellow 2...yellow 2...," followed by yells of success or groans of failure. =-) It is a very fun game which I give a solid 8.5.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

A luck filled SdJ nominee. Turn order seems to matter a lot. Components are nice, though.

RATING: 8
I don't put much stock in BGG rankings or various gaming awards, but in this case, the Spiel des Jahres has definitely picked a winner.  (I certainly can't think of a better family game for teaching children about the fun and rewarding experience that gambling provides!)  It's a very clever game centred around a very clever mechanism that is implemented using the brilliant dice pyramid.  The camels and all other components are well done too, and the game play is very simple and a lot of fun.  I particularly appreciate how the overall race is broken down into "legs", yet it all plays out quite quickly.  Luck is a factor as it is with any form of gambling, but the design is tight and it really is a good betting game.  The only real negative comment I can make is that, despite the fact that the game plays 2-8 players, I can see some game play problems cropping up outside the 3-5 players range (though my only plays so far have been 4-player games).  I give this game two humps up.  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 3.5/5  Total: 8/10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Players bet on camels racing around a track. A camel landing on a space where one already sits will land on top of it; the camel below will carry it if it moves subsequently. Each camel moves according to a die roll, with dice drawn in random order -- the result is that even a camel quite far behind may be able to race into first if it lands on another camel which then moves itself.

We played this immediately after Colt Express and the comparison is striking: Colt Express is chaotic, but the chaos is player-driven and there is a lot of fun in seeing clever schemes succeed or, more likely, fall apart. Camel Up, by contrast, is ultimately about betting on random dice rolls, and while there is some amusement at seeing a heavily-invested player losing bigtime it seems not to either their credit or disgrace. It's definitely got its moments, but most of the complexity (different kinds of betting, tiles to help/hinder camels) reads to me as providing decisions with the veneer of meaning but not its substance.

That offends me far more than a game with a similar level of randomness which does not pretend to be something that it isn't.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Quick playing race game where players have to bet on camels. The race is made up of five camels of different colours. On their turn players can perform one of a number of actions; either bet which camel will win a leg of the race (completed once all the camels have moved), bet which camel will win or come last in the overall race, place a tile that if landed on means the camels either move forward or backwards, or move the camels one to three spaces by using the dice from an upturned pyramid, which acts as a dice tower. The one original feature is that camels on the same space move together in a stack, so a camel on top of others has an advantage by being moved during the other camels' movements as well as its own. Whoever predicted winners/loser the best receives money (VPs) and whoever predicted wrongly has to pay. This game is more than a little mad and is certainly fun to play but I don't think it is as good as its Spiel des Jahres win would suggest and it is often over far too quickly.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
Ever since [thing=40237][/thing], I know that horse racing games can be fun for me. Most of them I don't enjoy, but I'm always willing to give them a shot. Even if they're themed to camels, not horses. This one involves a weird contraption shaped like a pyramid that you have to turn upside down to get a die from. I guess a drawbag and a die roll wasn't interesting enough.
Other than the fact that they're both racing and bidding games, there is not too much Camel Up and Long Shot have in common. This one is lighter and gives players less control over what happens.
I found that this game doesn't really work well with strategic players. I think it'll work better with families with kids. The problem is that the first turns every round you don't have any information to go on, so the only good move is to get a die. But after 2 or 3 dice, the next die will give away a lot of information, helping the player after the one drawing that die. So when that is you, you will have to either have a big chance of giving away the round to the next player (or at least helping in a significant way) or having to do something else, which will result in you taking a risk, which often is a crashoot. Which is why I feel this game doesn't work with strategic players who take notice of percentages of chances of things happening and stuff like that.

Initial rating: 6

RATING: N/A
Espace Jeux
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Camel Up (or is it Camel Cup?) is much more thoughtful than I anticipated. It is a type of horse (camel) racing game where the players are all attempting to pick the winners, both of individual legs of a race as well as the overall race. They can also try to manipulate the order of the camels in the race to a small degree. Fascinatingly, camels can stack and carry others along for a ride. This throws an interesting wrinkle into an otherwise straightforward race.

The game plays quickly, and it rides the line between giving the players too much knowledge about which camel is going to win (which would create an exercise in pure calculation) and no information at all (which would create a game of pure luck). In other words, there is just enough to keep things interesting. It is a worthy SdJ nomination with whimsical components. Played with a group in the mood for a bit of raucous fun, Camel Up even manages to transcend its roots as a family game and push into something party-worthy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5.5
[thing=153938][/thing] is a fun game, and it is pretty easy to learn: in your turn you have 4 things to do and you can do only one of them:
a) take a pyramid tile (is worth 1 money at the end of the leg) and roll the movement die for one of the camels;
b) take a bet tile for the leg (each is worth different: the first is worth 5, the second 3 and the third 2 money - so, the sooner you take them, the best is the reward, but if the camel you choose didn't finish the leg at least in second place, you lose 1 money. If the camel you pick a tile for finish in second, you get 1 money, no matter which tile you took). There are only three for each camel;
c) place a bet for the overall winner or the overall loser of the camels (it is allowed to place more than one bet of each type, but you will lose 1 money for each bet wrong). You place these bets hidden, but the cards must remain in the order they were put, since, in the end, the first player to bid in the correct winner or loser will gain 8 money, then, in order, 5, 3, 2 and 1 money;
d) place the tile of dry land (-1 movement) or oasis (+1 movement) in one spot in the race track. Everytime a camel step on your tile you gain 1 money.

If a camel enters in the same spot of other camel, it climbs on its back, and is considered to be ahead of the camel bellow it. If a camel bellow others move, it takes with him all camels above him. This is the key idea that drives the whole game. A leg lasts until the die for each camel has been rolled. After this, all bets tiles pay their rewards (or demand their penalties), each pyramid tile pays 1 money, and than a new leg starts. The game ends immediately when the first camel cross the finish line of the track. This is basically the all the game - easy, right?

I didn't like at all how the leg bets work - usually, after someone rolled a die, became obvious the one or two camels that would win the leg, so everyone else took the tiles of the bets, and when the game returned to the player that rolled the die, all the tiles for a given camel were taken. This happened in all the legs, in more or less severe ways. Sure, it could be because of how the camels started and the first ones to move were the ones ahead, so the "climbing" didn't happen as often as it could have been. I can imagine this, but I didn't saw this.

On the other hand, how the bets for the overall winner and loser I liked quite a bit - easy and tense at the same time, and since you can do more than one bet in both, even if your first one seems that won't pay out, you can place another bet (you will still lose one money for failed bet, but you can gain up to 8 for being the first to do the correct bet), and bidding on the loser camel was also a good addition. [thing=153938][/thing] is indeed mostly all about luck, however, it is also short enough for this didn't bother me at all.

The pieces are great and this will probably be a sure bet (a-ha) for a family game, as it is colorful, easy to teach and to play, with some minimal depth, making even the little ones a challenge in the game, and if they aren't, they will probably still have fun rolling the dice in the pyramid, ando also moving and stacking the camels. And, for those wandering, I think [thing=148228][/thing] is a better game, but is much drier and can't hold the 5 or 6 players that [thing=153938][/thing] can (but, more players in the game = bigger role for luck).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
Camel Up is a perfect example of why family games are awarded the SDJ and they often don't agree with BGG gamers. In reading the rule book, it is clear that the game is simple, straightforward and not burdened by complexity. Yet, behind the simple rule set is a more subtle but distinct strategy of risk-taking.

Yes, the heart of Camel Up is a racing game that involves dice and betting. However, the game play also provides ample time and space for smart play and calculated risk taking. For example, deciding when to play the desert/mirage tile allows you to help "surge" the camel of your choice ahead of the pack. Also, how the camel positions can easily change order.

 Strategies can backfire with poor die rolls, but it can be balanced with educated guesses and pondering probabilities...if you choose to do so. Some folks will certainly enjoy thinking about how to maximize risk taking while others will just enjoy using the inverted pyramid for rolling dice. Whether you choose one path or another, fun can be had by all. 

No, Camel Up won't win the IGA or DSP awards. But boy, this game sure hit the nail on its head with regards to being and SDJ winner. Kudos to
